## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: materials science - thermomechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material, which is a core constitutive modeling problem in materials science. Stress typically increases with strain (elasticity/hardening) and decreases with temperature (thermal softening), with possible nonlinear and coupled effects.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - c2 * T) (linear elasticity with temperature-dependent modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear stress-strain at constant temperature)
- Power-law with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - c3 * T) (hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook type: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T**c4) (combined hardening and thermal softening)
- Arrhenius thermal activation: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * (1/T)) (thermally activated deformation)
- Voce hardening with temperature: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)) * exp(c2 * (1/T)) (saturating hardening with Arrhenius softening)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic plus plastic contribution)
- Hollomon with thermal term: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(-c2 * T) (power hardening with exponential softening)
- Linear elastic-plastic: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T) (combined elastic-plastic with temperature dependence)
- Ludwik model with temperature: sigma = c0 * (c1 + epsilon)**c2 * exp(-c3 * T) (shifted power law with thermal softening)
- Swift hardening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * (c3 - c4 * T) (pre-strained power law with linear softening)
- Hyperbolic sine creep: sigma = c0 * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * (1/T))) (sinh-type flow stress model)
- Polynomial thermal modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (quadratic temperature-dependent modulus)
- Coupled power law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (power-law coupling of strain and temperature)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus → multiply strain term by a function of T (linear, polynomial, or exponential in T)
- Strain hardening saturation → use (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or tanh(c*epsilon) to capture Voce-type saturation behavior
- Arrhenius-type thermal activation → exp(c/T) or exp(-c*T) terms indicate thermally activated processes like dislocation glide
- Shifted power law (epsilon + c)^n → indicates pre-existing plastic strain or initial yield offset (Swift/Ludwik models)
- Homologous temperature scaling → (1 - (T/T_melt)^m) type terms represent fraction of melting temperature softening
- Strain-temperature coupling asymmetry → at high T, strain hardening exponent may decrease, suggesting n = f(T)
- Yield stress plus hardening decomposition → additive structure (c0 + c1*epsilon^c2) separating initial yield from work hardening
- Inverse temperature dependence → 1/T appearing in exponents suggests Boltzmann/Arrhenius statistical mechanics origin
